<p><b>Rafael "Rafa" Benítez Maudes</b> (<small>Spanish pronunciation: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Spanish" title="Help:IPA for Spanish">[rafaˈel ˈrafa βeˈniteθ ˈmauðes]</a></span>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> born 16 April 1960) is a Spanish <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> coach currently managing <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>. He is the only manager in history to have won the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a>, <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Super_Cup" title="UEFA Super Cup">UEFA Super Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> and the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="FIFA Club World Cup">FIFA Club World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Benítez joined <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a>'s coaching staff at the age of 26, going on to work as the under-19 and reserve team coach, and assistant manager for the senior team. Benítez moved away from Real Madrid, but management spells at <a href="/wiki/Real_Valladolid" title="Real Valladolid">Real Valladolid</a> and <a href="/wiki/CA_Osasuna" title="CA Osasuna">Osasuna</a> were short-lived and unsuccessful. Benítez guided <a href="/wiki/Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Segunda División">Segunda División</a> side <a href="/wiki/CF_Extremadura" title="CF Extremadura">Extremadura</a> back to the <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">Primera División</a> in his first season in <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="1997–98 Segunda División">1997</a>, but the team was relegated the following season. He left the club, and coached <a href="/wiki/CD_Tenerife" title="CD Tenerife">Tenerife</a> in 2000, winning promotion in <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="2000–01 Segunda División">his only season</a>.</p>
<p>Benítez was appointed coach of <a href="/wiki/Valencia_CF" title="Valencia CF">Valencia</a> and he proved himself to be amongst the top Spanish managers by winning <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_La_Liga" title="2001–02 La Liga">2001–02 season</a>. In 2004, another <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_La_Liga" title="2003–04 La Liga">La Liga league title</a> and a <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_UEFA_Cup" title="2003–04 UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a> victory were added.</p>
<p>Following his successful season, the Spaniard then moved to English club <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>, guiding the club to victory in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> in <a href="/wiki/2005_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2005 UEFA Champions League Final">2005</a>. For the second consecutive season, he was named <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Club_Football_Awards#Coach.28es.29_of_the_Year" title="UEFA Club Football Awards">UEFA Manager of the Year</a>. He also won the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/2006_FA_Cup_Final" title="2006 FA Cup Final">2006</a> and reached the <a href="/wiki/2007_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2007 UEFA Champions League Final">2007 Champions League Final</a>, but remained unable to win the Premier League, with Liverpool's best league performance under Benítez a second-place finish in <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Premier_League" title="2008–09 Premier League">2008–09</a>.</p>
<p>After leaving Liverpool in June 2010, Benítez managed <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a>, whom he guided to the <a href="/wiki/2010_Supercoppa_Italiana" title="2010 Supercoppa Italiana">Supercoppa Italiana</a> and <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA Club World Cup">FIFA Club World Cup</a> titles, but was dismissed midway through the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Serie_A" title="2010–11 Serie A">2010–11 season</a>. In November 2012 he was appointed interim manager of <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> for the remainder of the season, with which he won the <a href="/wiki/2013_UEFA_Europa_League_Final" title="2013 UEFA Europa League Final">2013 Europa League</a>.</p>
<p>Benítez returned to Italy in 2013 to coach <a href="/wiki/S.S.C._Napoli" title="S.S.C. Napoli">Napoli</a>, where he won the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Coppa_Italia" title="2013–14 Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> and <a href="/wiki/2014_Supercoppa_Italiana" title="2014 Supercoppa Italiana">Supercoppa Italiana</a>. Benítez then left Napoli and became coach of <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> in June 2015 on an initial three-year contract. On 4 January 2016, however, he was dismissed following a 2–2 draw against Valencia, with Real Madrid third in La Liga behind <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a>.</p>
<p>On 11 March 2016, Benítez was announced as the manager of <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span></h2>
<p>Benítez passed through the playing ranks as a midfielder for both <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C" title="Real Madrid C">Real Madrid Aficionados</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Tercera_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Tercera División">Tercera División</a> and <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_Castilla" title="Real Madrid Castilla">Castilla CF</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Segunda División">Segunda División</a>. He also enrolled as a student at INEF, the sports faculty at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universidad_Polit%C3%A9cnica_de_Madrid" title="Universidad Politécnica de Madrid">Universidad Politécnica de Madrid</a> and in 1982 he obtained a degree in physical education.</p>
<p>In 1979, Benítez was selected to play for the Spain Youth U-19s at the <a href="/wiki/Universiade" title="Universiade">World Student Games</a> in Mexico City and he scored a penalty in the opening game, a 10–0 win against Cuba. In the next game, a 0–0 draw against Canada, he was injured in a hard tackle. The injury saw him sidelined for a year which realistically ended his chances of becoming a major player. In 1981, Benítez joined <a href="/wiki/Tercera_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Tercera División">Tercera División</a> side <a href="/wiki/AD_Parla" title="AD Parla">Parla</a>. Initially, he joined Parla on loan, but eventually signed for them permanently and helped them gain promotion to <a href="/wiki/Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n_B" title="Segunda División B">Segunda División B</a>. He also played a further three games for the Spain Universities XI. In 1985 he signed for Segunda División B club <a href="/wiki/Linares_CF" title="Linares CF">Linares</a> and under <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Mateos" title="Enrique Mateos">Enrique Mateos</a>, he served as a player/coach. Further injury problems saw him miss almost the entire 1985–86 season and he subsequently retired as a player.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bio_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bio-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Managerial_career">Managerial career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Real_Madrid_youth_coach">Real Madrid youth coach</span></h3>
<p>In 1986, at the age of 26, Benítez returned to <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> to join the club's coaching staff. At the start of the 1986–87 season, he was appointed coach of <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_Castilla" title="Real Madrid Castilla">Castilla B</a>. With this team, he won two league titles in 1987 and 1989. He won a third league title with <i>Real Madrid Youth B</i> in 1990. Halfway through the 1990–91 season he succeeded <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Antonio_Camacho" title="José Antonio Camacho">José Antonio Camacho</a> as the coach of Real Madrid' under-19 club. With the team, he won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spain_U-19_Cup" title="Spain U-19 Cup">Spain Under 19s Cup</a> in 1991 and 1993, defeating <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> in both finals. In 1993, the team completed a <a href="/wiki/Double_(association_football)" title="Double (association football)">double</a> when they also won the <a href="/wiki/Divisi%C3%B3n_de_Honor_Juvenil_de_F%C3%BAtbol" title="División de Honor Juvenil de Fútbol">national under-19 league</a>. While at Real, Benítez also gained his coaching certificate in 1989 and in the summer of 1990 taught at a football camp at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Davis" title="University of California, Davis">University of California, Davis</a>, in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>.</p>
<p>During the 1992–93 season, Benítez also worked as an assistant coach to <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Garc%C3%ADa_Rem%C3%B3n" title="Mariano García Remón">Mariano García Remón</a> at Real Madrid B. After his success with the U19s, Benítez then succeeded García Remón at the start of the 1993–94 season. Real Madrid B were then playing in the <a href="/wiki/Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Segunda División">Segunda División</a> and on 4 September 1993, he made his debut as a Segunda División manager with a 3–1 over <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A9rcules_CF" title="Hércules CF">Hércules</a>. In March 1994, he became assistant manager to <a href="/wiki/Vicente_del_Bosque" title="Vicente del Bosque">Vicente del Bosque</a> with the senior Real Madrid team before returning to coach Real Madrid B for the 1994–95 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bio_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bio-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_coaching">Early coaching</span></h3>
<p>The first attempts by Benítez at senior management away from the Real Madrid fold were less than successful. He was appointed manager of <a href="/wiki/Real_Valladolid" title="Real Valladolid">Real Valladolid</a> for the <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_La_Liga" title="1995–96 La Liga">1995–96 season</a>, but was sacked after only two wins in 23 games with the club bottom of the <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">Primera División</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="1996–97 Segunda División">1996–97 season</a>, Benítez took charge at <a href="/wiki/CA_Osasuna" title="CA Osasuna">Osasuna</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Segunda División">Segunda División</a>, but after only nine games and one win, he was sacked. He did, however, meet the fitness instructor <a href="/wiki/Pako_Ayestar%C3%A1n" title="Pako Ayestarán">Pako Ayestarán</a> at the club, and went on to form a partnership with him at several clubs for the next decade. In 1997, he joined another Segunda División side, <a href="/wiki/CF_Extremadura" title="CF Extremadura">Extremadura</a>, and this time led them to promotion, finishing second in the table behind <a href="/wiki/Deportivo_Alav%C3%A9s" title="Deportivo Alavés">Deportivo Alavés</a> after winning 23 out of 42 games. Extremadura only survived one season in Primera División, however, and were relegated in 1999 after finishing 17th and losing a play-off to <a href="/wiki/Villarreal_CF" title="Villarreal CF">Villarreal</a>.</p>
<p>Benítez subsequently quit Extremadura and took a year off from football to study in England and Italy. He also worked as a commentator/analyst for <a href="/wiki/Eurosport" title="Eurosport">Eurosport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marca_(newspaper)" title="Marca (newspaper)"><i>Marca</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Mundo_(Spain)" title="El Mundo (Spain)"><i>El Mundo</i></a> and local Madrid TV. In 2000, he was appointed manager of <a href="/wiki/CD_Tenerife" title="CD Tenerife">Tenerife</a> of the Segunda División and with a team that included <a href="/wiki/Mista_(footballer)" title="Mista (footballer)">Mista</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curro_Torres" title="Curro Torres">Curro Torres</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luis_Garc%C3%ADa_(footballer,_born_1978)" title="Luis García (footballer, born 1978)">Luis García</a>, he gained promotion to <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a> by finishing third in the league behind <a href="/wiki/Sevilla_FC" title="Sevilla FC">Sevilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Real_Betis" title="Real Betis">Real Betis</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Valencia">Valencia</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2001.E2.80.9304_Spanish_champions_and_UEFA_Cup_winners">2001–04 Spanish champions and UEFA Cup winners</span></h4>
<p>In 2001, Benítez was appointed coach of <a href="/wiki/Valencia_CF" title="Valencia CF">Valencia</a>, replacing <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A9ctor_C%C3%BAper" title="Héctor Cúper">Héctor Cúper</a>. The club had previously approached <a href="/wiki/Javier_Irureta" title="Javier Irureta">Javier Irureta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Esnal" title="José Manuel Esnal">Mané</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luis_Aragon%C3%A9s" title="Luis Aragonés">Luis Aragonés</a> and had been turned down by all three. However, Club Director Javier Subirats recognised the potential of Benítez and campaigned for his appointment. Despite the loss of <a href="/wiki/Gaizka_Mendieta" title="Gaizka Mendieta">Gaizka Mendieta</a>, Benítez inherited from Cúper a team brimming with potential, with <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Ca%C3%B1izares" title="Santiago Cañizares">Santiago Cañizares</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Ayala" title="Roberto Ayala">Roberto Ayala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rub%C3%A9n_Baraja" title="Rubén Baraja">Rubén Baraja</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Albelda" title="David Albelda">David Albelda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Vicente Rodríguez">Vicente</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Aimar" title="Pablo Aimar">Pablo Aimar</a> providing the backbone to a formidable side that had reached back-to-back <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> finals in <a href="/wiki/2000_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2000 UEFA Champions League Final">2000</a> and <a href="/wiki/2001_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2001 UEFA Champions League Final">2001</a>.</p>
<p>Valencia fans were soon won over by Benítez after he introduced a more attacking style of play than his predecessor, Cúper. He also brought in both Mista from his former club and <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Rufete" title="Francisco Rufete">Francisco Rufete</a> from <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga_CF" title="Málaga CF">Málaga</a>, with Mista going on to become top goalscorer for Valencia with 19 goals in the <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_La_Liga" title="2003–04 La Liga">2003–04 season</a>. In 2002, these tactics saw Benítez lead Valencia to their first Liga title in 31 years, winning it by a seven-point margin over second-placed <a href="/wiki/Deportivo_de_La_Coru%C3%B1a" title="Deportivo de La Coruña">Deportivo La Coruña</a>.</p>
<p>However, the following <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_La_Liga" title="2002–03 La Liga">2002–03 season</a> was a disappointing one—the club failed to follow up on their title success, finishing fifth in La Liga, 18 points behind champions Real Madrid. The season saw Benítez make his debut in the <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2002–03 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a>, where his side reached the quarter-finals, losing to <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a>.</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_La_Liga" title="2003–04 La Liga">2003–04 season</a>, Valencia won La Liga with three games to spare and beat <a href="/wiki/Olympique_de_Marseille" title="Olympique de Marseille">Marseille</a> 2–0 in the <a href="/wiki/2004_UEFA_Cup_Final" title="2004 UEFA Cup Final">UEFA Cup final</a>. Despite this success, Benítez fell out with <a href="/wiki/Jes%C3%BAs_Garc%C3%ADa_Pitarch" title="Jesús García Pitarch">Jesús García Pitarch</a>, the club's <a href="/wiki/Director_of_football" title="Director of football">director of football</a>, over control of new signings and the club's failure to reinforce the squad with the players he wanted. He famously said, "I was hoping for a sofa [a defender] and they've brought me a lamp <a href="/wiki/Fabi%C3%A1n_Canobbio" title="Fabián Canobbio">[Fabián Canobbio]</a>," in reference to the <a href="/wiki/Association_football_positions" title="Association football positions">positions</a> he wanted to be strengthened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> These differences of opinion saw Benítez resign as Valencia coach in June 2004.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liverpool">Liverpool</span></h3>
<p>On 16 June 2004, Benítez was appointed manager of <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>, becoming the first Spaniard to manage in the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2004.E2.80.9306_Early_successes">2004–06 Early successes</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rafael_Benitez.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="688" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Rafael_Benitez.JPG/222px-Rafael_Benitez.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Rafael_Benitez.JPG/333px-Rafael_Benitez.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Rafael_Benitez.JPG/444px-Rafael_Benitez.JPG 2x" width="222"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rafael_Benitez.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rafael Benítez managing Liverpool against <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a> in 2005</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>One of Benítez's first tasks at Liverpool was to convince club captain <a href="/wiki/Steven_Gerrard" title="Steven Gerrard">Steven Gerrard</a> not to move to rivals <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> He was unable, however, to convince <a href="/wiki/Michael_Owen" title="Michael Owen">Michael Owen</a> to extend his contract; he was subsequently sold to Real Madrid. Later in the summer transfer window, Benítez signed several players from La Liga, most notably Luis García and <a href="/wiki/Xabi_Alonso" title="Xabi Alonso">Xabi Alonso</a>, both of whom drew immediate admiration from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kopites" title="Kopites">Kopites</a>. Benítez also gave new life to existing Liverpool players, transforming <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Carragher" title="Jamie Carragher">Jamie Carragher</a> from a utility player to one of Europe's top centre backs<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> alongside <a href="/wiki/Sami_Hyypi%C3%A4" title="Sami Hyypiä">Sami Hyypiä</a>.</p>
<p>During his first season, Benítez failed to improve Liverpool's form in the Premiership. Key players missed much of the season through injury and Liverpool failed to challenge Chelsea and <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> for the league title, finishing fifth. Benítez, however, did reach his first English domestic cup final, losing the <a href="/wiki/2005_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2005 Football League Cup Final">League Cup final</a> against Chelsea at the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a> 3–2 after extra time.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2004–05 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a>, however, Liverpool fared differently, despite their poor start. Liverpool began their campaign with an unimpressive 2–1 aggregate win over <a href="/wiki/Grazer_AK" title="Grazer AK">Grazer AK</a> in the qualifying rounds and were minutes away from going out of the competition in the group stages. However, an 87th-minute goal by Steven Gerrard defeated <a href="/wiki/Olympiacos_F.C." title="Olympiacos F.C.">Olympiacos</a> 3–1 and saw the club progress to the last 16 on head-to-head difference. After defeating <a href="/wiki/Bayer_04_Leverkusen" title="Bayer 04 Leverkusen">Bayer Leverkusen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> with the aid of some bold team selections by Benítez, Liverpool faced Chelsea in the semi-final. A controversial early goal from Luis García saw Liverpool win 1–0 on aggregate and reach <a href="/wiki/2005_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2005 UEFA Champions League Final">the final</a> against <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">Milan</a>.</p>
<p>In a classic final, Liverpool came from 3–0 down at half time to level the score at 3–3 in the space of just six minutes, eventually triumphing 3–2 on penalties with the assistance of goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Jerzy_Dudek" title="Jerzy Dudek">Jerzy Dudek</a>. Benítez's calm, methodical approach at half time was said to give the players the belief they could pull off an improbable comeback and win Liverpool an historic fifth European Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> In doing so, Benítez became only the third manager in history (after <a href="/wiki/Bob_Paisley" title="Bob Paisley">Bob Paisley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mourinho" title="José Mourinho">José Mourinho</a>) to win the UEFA Cup and UEFA Champions League in successive seasons, and the second Liverpool manager (after <a href="/wiki/Joe_Fagan" title="Joe Fagan">Joe Fagan</a>) ever to win the European Cup/UEFA Champions League in his first season in charge. Benítez's tactics were credited as a key factor in Liverpool reaching, and winning, the final, despite a relatively unimpressive squad of players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>It is notable that Dudek's heroics in the final were not enough for him to stay as first-choice keeper, as newly-signed <a href="/wiki/Pepe_Reina" title="Pepe Reina">Pepe Reina</a> replaced him in from the start of the 2005–06 season. Benítez also quickly discarded unlikely heroes <a href="/wiki/Vladim%C3%ADr_%C5%A0micer" title="Vladimír Šmicer">Vladimír Šmicer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Igor_Bi%C5%A1%C4%87an" title="Igor Bišćan">Igor Bišćan</a>, who played key roles in the European success but seemingly did not figure in Benítez's long-term plans. Benítez also quickly sold <a href="/wiki/Josemi" title="Josemi">Josemi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antonio_N%C3%BA%C3%B1ez_Tena" title="Antonio Núñez Tena">Antonio Núñez</a>, two of his first signings in English football, after they failed to establish themselves, with the likes of <a href="/wiki/Peter_Crouch" title="Peter Crouch">Peter Crouch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Sissoko" title="Mohamed Sissoko">Mohamed Sissoko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Agger" title="Daniel Agger">Daniel Agger</a> as well as former Liverpool player (and fan favourite) <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Fowler" title="Robbie Fowler">Robbie Fowler</a> being brought in to strengthen the side.</p>
<p>Benítez's signings helped the club's Premiership form improve considerably. Liverpool finished third in the league, missing out on second place by one point. Liverpool also won the <a href="/wiki/2006_FA_Cup_Final" title="2006 FA Cup Final">FA Cup</a> beating both <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> and Chelsea, as well as a thrilling 5–3 win against <a href="/wiki/Luton_Town_F.C." title="Luton Town F.C.">Luton Town</a> in the third round, on the way to the final against <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a>. History repeated itself in the final as they then went on to lift the trophy after a penalty shoot-out, following a dramatic 3–3 draw. Liverpool came from 2–0 down and were losing 3–2 in stoppage time when Steven Gerrard scored a dramatic late equalizer. This time, Pepe Reina saved three penalties during the shoot-out to secure the silverware. In winning the FA Cup, Benítez became the only manager in Liverpool's history to win major trophies in both of his first two seasons at the club.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2006.E2.80.9308_Confrontation_with_new_owners">2006–08 Confrontation with new owners</span></h4>
<p>Following Benítez's great early success, the English media were predicting Liverpool would challenge Chelsea for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Premier_League" title="2006–07 Premier League">2006–07 Premier League</a> title after Benítez addressed Liverpool's perceived weaknesses in the transfer window, a belief reaffirmed after his side won the <a href="/wiki/FA_Community_Shield" title="FA Community Shield">Community Shield</a> with a 2–1 victory over Chelsea. The title challenge, however, fizzled out early in the season, with Liverpool's poor form away from <a href="/wiki/Anfield" title="Anfield">Anfield</a> leading to speculation Benítez's tenure at Liverpool was short-lived, with his agent quoted as saying Benítez would consider offers to manage in Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Benítez swiftly issued a statement through the club's website re-affirming his desire to remain with Liverpool for the long-term.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> In January, Benítez's side lost twice in four days to Arsenal in both domestic cup competitions, including a 6–3 defeat in the League Cup that was Liverpool's heaviest home defeat since 1913. Despite the poor domestic performances, Liverpool fans remained supportive of Benítez.</p>
<p>Supporters and manager joined together to welcome new owners <a href="/wiki/George_N._Gillett_Jr." title="George N. Gillett Jr.">George Gillett</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hicks" title="Tom Hicks">Tom Hicks</a>, with the hope the new owners would bring funding for new players and a new stadium. Gillett declared himself delighted with the manager of his new investment, as Benítez overcame his domestic difficulties to lead Liverpool to another <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2006–07 UEFA Champions League">Champions League final</a>. After Liverpool again defeated Chelsea in the semi-final, this time on penalties, Gillett stated, "Rafa has been tremendous ... We knew of him but I don't think we realized how good he was, and not just as a coach. Not only was he a brilliant coach but he is a very sharp, savvy businessman. He knows what he wants and how to get it. The more we have seen of him the more impressed we have become."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Benítez did not reciprocate his owner's kind words, demanding his club's new owners had to back him in the transfer market in order for Liverpool to progress following his side's 2–1 loss to Milan in the final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> It was reported Benítez did not feel he had the complete support of the new owners, a thought that was compounded by Liverpool's initial lack of activity in the transfer window, although the club played these rumours down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Benítez's spending was, eventually, significant, breaking Liverpool's transfer record when signing Spanish striker <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Torres" title="Fernando Torres">Fernando Torres</a> from <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a> as well as signing <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Babel" title="Ryan Babel">Ryan Babel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yossi_Benayoun" title="Yossi Benayoun">Yossi Benayoun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Leiva" title="Lucas Leiva">Lucas Leiva</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andriy_Voronin" title="Andriy Voronin">Andriy Voronin</a>. Among those Benítez sold was <a href="/wiki/Craig_Bellamy" title="Craig Bellamy">Craig Bellamy</a>, who was notably phased out of the first team following an altercation with <a href="/wiki/John_Arne_Riise" title="John Arne Riise">John Arne Riise</a> in the buildup to Liverpool's remarkable victory over Barcelona in the <a href="/wiki/Camp_Nou" title="Camp Nou">Camp Nou</a> en route to the Champions League final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Liverpool made a good start to the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Premier_League" title="2007–08 Premier League">2007–08 season</a>, topping the Premier League table for the first time under Benítez after a comprehensive 6–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Derby_County_F.C." title="Derby County F.C.">Derby County</a>. Despite this, poor results in the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2007–08 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> and a disagreement over future transfers lead to a public falling-out with the club's owners, which played out in the media at the end of November. It was suggested that Benítez's position was now under serious threat. The resulting coverage resulted in a show of support by fans in support of Benítez which culminated in a fans' march in support of Benítez ahead of the critical Champions League home tie with <a href="/wiki/FC_Porto" title="FC Porto">Porto</a>, which they won 4–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> It later emerged that <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Klinsmann" title="Jürgen Klinsmann">Jürgen Klinsmann</a> had been offered Benítez's job before eventually accepting the post of <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a> manager. Such a revelation damaged Benítez's relations with the Americans, with constant rumours linking the Spaniard with a move back to Real Madrid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Benítez, however, insisted his future was at Liverpool and signalled his long-term intentions by appointing <a href="/wiki/Sammy_Lee_(footballer)" title="Sammy Lee (footballer)">Sammy Lee</a> as his new assistant<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> to replace his long-time right-hand man, Pako Ayestarán, who quit after a reported disagreement, which Benítez admitted "hurt" him and arguably Liverpool's titles hopes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>Benítez was unable to win any trophies as Liverpool's domestic campaign falter in the winter months – including a shock FA Cup exit at home to <a href="/wiki/Barnsley_F.C." title="Barnsley F.C.">Barnsley</a>, with his side losing to Chelsea in the Champions League semi-finals. Despite the lack of silverware, the main talking points were off the pitch, with Benítez in the middle of a power struggle with the Liverpool board.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2008.E2.80.9309_League_runner-up">2008–09 League runner-up</span></h4>
<p>In a sign of the increasingly strained relationship between the Liverpool manager and his board, Benítez was reportedly close to quitting Liverpool in the summer of 2008 over the Liverpool board's failure to back him in his bid to purchase <a href="/wiki/Gareth_Barry" title="Gareth Barry">Gareth Barry</a> from <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Benítez had reportedly intended to sell Xabi Alonso to fund the purchase of Barry, but Liverpool <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CEO" title="CEO">CEO</a> <a href="/wiki/Rick_Parry" title="Rick Parry">Rick Parry</a> was reported to have prioritised signing <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Keane" title="Robbie Keane">Robbie Keane</a> over Barry, causing tension when Barry did not arrive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Striker Keane was later re-sold back to <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> in the January transfer window, with some analysts claiming he was a "pawn in a power struggle" between Benítez and the club's owners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> This off-field turmoil was in contrast to Liverpool's impressive start to the 2008–09 season in the Premier League, including Benítez' first ever league win against Manchester United at Anfield on 13 September and ending Chelsea's 86 match unbeaten run in the league at <a href="/wiki/Stamford_Bridge_(stadium)" title="Stamford Bridge (stadium)">Stamford Bridge</a>. Liverpool finished the calendar year top of the Premier League for the first time since 1996.</p>
<p>However, Liverpool's poor results in the New Year led to a sharper focus on Benítez, who had missed Liverpool's draw at Arsenal in December due to an operation to remove <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kidney_stones" title="Kidney stones">kidney stones</a>. An infamous attack on Manchester United boss <a href="/wiki/Alex_Ferguson" title="Alex Ferguson">Sir Alex Ferguson</a> in the media led some pundits and opposition supporters to suggest Benítez was "cracking up" under the pressure of a title bid. Benítez still appeared to be at odds with Liverpool's owners, publicly turning down a contract extension and demanding more control over transfers. At one point, rumours of Benítez quitting or being sacked became so great that bookmakers had to suspend betting on the subject.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-betting1_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-betting1-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Nevertheless, on 18 March 2009, shortly after registering a 4–0 victory over Real Madrid and 4–1 victory over Manchester United, Benítez signed a new five-year deal with the club. Benítez said, "My heart is with Liverpool, so I'm delighted to sign this new deal, I love the club, the fans and the city and with a club and supporters like this, I could never say no to staying."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newdeal_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-newdeal-27">[27]</a></sup> With ten wins in their last 11 games, Liverpool finished the season on a high, finishing second in the league for the first time under Benítez, four points off champions Manchester United, with Liverpool playing an attractive brand of attacking football at odds with the side that struggled through the winter months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2009.E2.80.9310:_Decline_and_dismissal">2009–10: Decline and dismissal</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:335px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rafael_Benitez_2009_Asia_Tour.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="515" data-file-width="772" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Rafael_Benitez_2009_Asia_Tour.jpg/333px-Rafael_Benitez_2009_Asia_Tour.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Rafael_Benitez_2009_Asia_Tour.jpg/500px-Rafael_Benitez_2009_Asia_Tour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Rafael_Benitez_2009_Asia_Tour.jpg/666px-Rafael_Benitez_2009_Asia_Tour.jpg 2x" width="333"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rafael_Benitez_2009_Asia_Tour.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rafael Benítez during Liverpool's Asia Tour in 2009.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Fans were hopeful with Benítez's long-term future sorted Liverpool could push on to the next level in the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Premier_League" title="2009–10 Premier League">2009–10 season</a> and win their first League title in 20 years. The season that followed, however, resulted in Liverpool finishing in seventh and Benítez's contract being terminated by mutual consent.</p>
<p>Prior to Benítez's final season, Xabi Alonso, one of the key members of Benítez's squad, was sold to Real Madrid following a lengthy pursuit in a deal reportedly worth £30 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Alonso admitted that Benítez's attempts to sell him the previous summer were a deciding factor in his move.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Alonso was immediately replaced in the squad by Italian midfielder <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Aquilani" title="Alberto Aquilani">Alberto Aquilani</a>, signed from <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">Roma</a> for £17 million, who was recovering from a long-term injury. Also added was England defender <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glen_Johnson_(English_footballer)" title="Glen Johnson (English footballer)">Glen Johnson</a> for a £17.5 million fee. A "sell to buy" policy enforced by the ownership due to increasing debt, combined with Alonso's departure, prompted discontent amongst considerable sections of the club's fanbase who believed Benítez was not being backed sufficiently in the transfer market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Benítez's decision to sell Alonso and replace him in the side with Lucas Leiva, in addition to Aquilani having arrived at the club injured, was called into question as Liverpool's title campaign began with two defeats in the first three games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Benítez defended his decisions, arguing Liverpool's slow start was due to key players such as Steven Gerrard being below par.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Liverpool's worst run in 22 years<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> combined with an exit from the Champions League at the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_UEFA_Champions_League_group_stage" title="2009–10 UEFA Champions League group stage">group stages</a> led to the first major vocal criticism of Benítez by Liverpool fans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> It was suggested that this Liverpool team was missing Benítez's characteristic defensive rigidness<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> despite the fact that only Manchester United and Chelsea conceded fewer goals than Liverpool, and lacked the necessary depth to cope with injuries to key players such as Gerrard and Fernando Torres while Benítez's decision making was called into question.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The club subsequently exited the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> at the hands of <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a>, eliminating any hope of a trophy.</p>
<p>Benítez left the club "by mutual consent" on 3 June 2010<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RBLL_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-RBLL-38">[38]</a></sup> with a reported £6 million pay-off;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> the media speculated that this was because the team had finished seventh in the Premier League, missing out on the Champions League, and suffered poor results, including the defeat by <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Athletic_F.C." title="Wigan Athletic F.C.">Wigan Athletic</a>. Shortly after his departure from Anfield, Benítez made a £96,000 donation to the Hillsborough Family Support Group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inter_Milan">Inter Milan</span></h3>
<p>On 10 June 2010, and only a few days after leaving Liverpool, Benítez agreed a deal to become the new head coach of <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> and reigning <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2009–10 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> title-holders <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a>, a post that was left vacant by the departure of José Mourinho, who left to manage Real Madrid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> On 15 June 2010, Benítez was presented to the Italian media for the first time after signing a two-year deal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> On 21 August 2010, Benítez won his first trophy as manager, the <a href="/wiki/Supercoppa_Italiana" title="Supercoppa Italiana">Italian Super Cup</a>, after they defeated Roma 3–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> On 27 August 2010 in <a href="/wiki/Stade_Louis_II" title="Stade Louis II">Monaco</a>, Inter lost to Atlético Madrid in the <a href="/wiki/2010_UEFA_Super_Cup" title="2010 UEFA Super Cup">2010 UEFA Super Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Benítez's first <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Serie_A" title="2010–11 Serie A">Serie A</a> game in charge was on 31 August 2010 in a 0–0 draw away to <a href="/wiki/Bologna_F.C._1909" title="Bologna F.C. 1909">Bologna</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Stadio_Renato_Dall%27Ara" title="Stadio Renato Dall'Ara">Stadio Renato Dall'Ara</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> His first league win as manager came on 11 September 2010, a 2–1 win against <a href="/wiki/Udinese_Calcio" title="Udinese Calcio">Udinese</a> at the <a href="/wiki/San_Siro" title="San Siro">San Siro</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>By December 2010, Inter had slumped to sixth in Serie A, 13 points adrift of the top (although Inter played two games less), having suffered consecutive defeats against <a href="/wiki/Derby_della_Madonnina" title="Derby della Madonnina">arch rivals</a> Milan (which ended a 46 match unbeaten home record),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A.C._Chievo_Verona" title="A.C. Chievo Verona">Chievo</a> and <a href="/wiki/S.S._Lazio" title="S.S. Lazio">Lazio</a>, as well as losing at Tottenham Hotspur in the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2010–11 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a>, leading to speculation that Benítez's position was under threat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Despite criticism, Benítez guided Inter to win the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA Club World Cup">FIFA Club World Cup</a> in December 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Buoyed by the Club World Cup victory, he told the European champions to back him with new signings or consider whether they wanted to keep him as coach, despite the side having <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Inter_Milan_season" title="2009–10 Inter Milan season">won the treble only a few months earlier</a>. Benítez's demands were dismissed out of hand by the Inter ownership, with <a href="/wiki/Massimo_Moratti" title="Massimo Moratti">Massimo Moratti</a> refusing to comment Benítez's continued employment by the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> On 23 December, Benítez was sacked by Inter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chelsea">Chelsea</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rafaelbenitez.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2208" data-file-width="1800" height="272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Rafaelbenitez.jpg/222px-Rafaelbenitez.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Rafaelbenitez.jpg/333px-Rafaelbenitez.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Rafaelbenitez.jpg/444px-Rafaelbenitez.jpg 2x" width="222"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rafaelbenitez.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rafael Benítez managing Chelsea against <a href="/wiki/FC_Nordsj%C3%A6lland" title="FC Nordsjælland">Nordsjælland</a> in 2012.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 21 November 2012, following the sacking of <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Di_Matteo" title="Roberto Di Matteo">Roberto Di Matteo</a>, Chelsea appointed Benítez as interim first-team manager until the end of the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Premier_League" title="2012–13 Premier League">2012–13 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> He was unveiled as the new Chelsea manager at a press conference on 22 November 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> He appointed <a href="/wiki/Boudewijn_Zenden" title="Boudewijn Zenden">Boudewijn Zenden</a> as his new assistant manager at Chelsea on the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>The appointment was unpopular with many Chelsea fans due to Benítez' association with Liverpool and comments he had previously made about the club,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> and he received a "fiercely hostile reception" as he was introduced at his first home game, a 0–0 draw with <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> on 25 November 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> This was followed by a 0–0 draw at home to <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a> and a 3–1 loss to West Ham.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> On 5 December 2012, Benítez recorded his first win as Chelsea manager, a 6–1 victory at home to <a href="/wiki/FC_Nordsj%C3%A6lland" title="FC Nordsjælland">Nordsjælland</a> in the Champions League. Despite this win, Chelsea failed to progress beyond the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_UEFA_Champions_League_group_stage#Group_E" title="2012–13 UEFA Champions League group stage">group stage</a> of the competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> This was followed by a 3–1 away victory to <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a>, with Benítez presiding over his first league win as Chelsea manager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2538" data-file-width="1800" height="313" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez.jpg/222px-Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez.jpg/333px-Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez.jpg/444px-Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez.jpg 2x" width="222"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Benítez in 2012.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/2012_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2012 FIFA Club World Cup">FIFA Club World Cup</a> in December 2012, Chelsea defeated <a href="/wiki/C.F._Monterrey" title="C.F. Monterrey">Monterrey</a> 3–1 to reach the final,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> where they were beaten 1–0 by Brazilian side <a href="/wiki/Sport_Club_Corinthians_Paulista" title="Sport Club Corinthians Paulista">Corinthians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Chelsea progressed to the League Cup semi-finals with a 5–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a> at <a href="/wiki/Elland_Road" title="Elland Road">Elland Road</a> and then recorded an 8–0 win over Aston Villa, equalling their record top-flight victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> They subsequently lost 1–0 at home to 20th-placed <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> in the Premier League and were knocked out of the League Cup semi-finals by underdogs <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a> 2–0 on aggregate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rafael_Benitez.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="519" data-file-width="401" height="287" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Rafael_Benitez.jpg/222px-Rafael_Benitez.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Rafael_Benitez.jpg/333px-Rafael_Benitez.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/16/Rafael_Benitez.jpg 2x" width="222"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rafael_Benitez.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Benítez with Chelsea in 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 27 February 2013, following a 2–0 win at <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a> in the FA Cup fifth-round, Benítez heavily criticised the Chelsea board for giving him the title of "interim manager" and the Chelsea fans for their protests against him. He also confirmed that he would be leaving the club at the end of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> He described his relationship with Chelsea owner <a href="/wiki/Roman_Abramovich" title="Roman Abramovich">Roman Abramovich</a> as "excellent" and expressed his desire to remain as Chelsea manager until the end of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Results continued to be mixed, and at one point Chelsea found themselves 16 points behind league leaders Manchester United, having been just four behind when Benítez was appointed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Chelsea reached the semi-finals of the FA Cup, losing 2–1 to Manchester City at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>, and also progressed to the final of the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2012–13 UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a>. In the penultimate league game of the season, Chelsea won 2–1 away to Aston Villa, a game in which <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lampard" title="Frank Lampard">Frank Lampard</a> set the all-time scoring record at Chelsea. The win secured a top-four Premiership finish and with it a place in the following season's <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2013–14 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2013_UEFA_Europa_League_Final" title="2013 UEFA Europa League Final">Europa League Final</a> against <a href="/wiki/S.L._Benfica" title="S.L. Benfica">Benfica</a> on 15 May, Chelsea won 2–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> This made Benítez only the second manager after <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Trapattoni" title="Giovanni Trapattoni">Giovanni Trapattoni</a> to have won the UEFA Cup/Europa League with two different teams, and Chelsea became the fourth club to have won all three of UEFA's major club competitions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Defender <a href="/wiki/David_Luiz" title="David Luiz">David Luiz</a> credited Benítez with making critical changes at half time, saying, "He changed some of our positions in the second half. That's why we played better and won the title. He spoke a lot to us to change the intensity." On the winning goal scored by <a href="/wiki/Branislav_Ivanovi%C4%87" title="Branislav Ivanović">Branislav Ivanović</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Mata" title="Juan Mata">Juan Mata</a> said, "Rafa told us we had to aim to the far post, because it was <a href="/wiki/Artur_Moraes" title="Artur Moraes">Artur</a>'s weakest place. I just tried to put the ball there and Ivanovic did the rest."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 19 May, in his final competitive game as Chelsea manager, Benítez managed the team to a 2–1 home win over <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a>, ensuring a third-place finish in the Premier League and a direct spot in the following season's Champions League group stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Napoli">Napoli</span></h3>
<p>On 27 May 2013, it was announced that Benítez had signed for <a href="/wiki/S.S.C._Napoli" title="S.S.C. Napoli">Napoli</a>, whose manager <a href="/wiki/Walter_Mazzarri" title="Walter Mazzarri">Walter Mazzarri</a> had resigned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Benítez agreed a two-year contract after meeting club president <a href="/wiki/Aurelio_De_Laurentiis" title="Aurelio De Laurentiis">Aurelio De Laurentiis</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>In his <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_S.S.C._Napoli_season" title="2013–14 S.S.C. Napoli season">first season</a> in charge, Benítez guided the club to victory in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Coppa_Italia" title="2013–14 Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a>, defeating <a href="/wiki/ACF_Fiorentina" title="ACF Fiorentina">Fiorentina</a> 3–1 in the final,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> and into the last 16 of the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2013–14 UEFA Europa League">Europa League</a>, exiting after a 3–2 aggregate defeat to Porto.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Napoli finished third in Serie A in <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Serie_A" title="2013–14 Serie A">2013–14</a> to qualify for the next season's <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2014–15 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> They lost 4–2 on aggregate to <a href="/wiki/Athletic_Bilbao" title="Athletic Bilbao">Athletic Bilbao</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_UEFA_Champions_League_qualifying_phase_and_play-off_round#Play-off_round" title="2014–15 UEFA Champions League qualifying phase and play-off round">qualifying stages</a>, thus entering the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2014–15 UEFA Europa League">Europa League</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>Benítez announced that he would resign at the end of the 2014–15 season. His final match was a 4–2 defeat to Lazio, who took the final place in the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2015–16 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> at Napoli's expense.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Real_Madrid">Real Madrid</span></h3>
<table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wikinews-logo.svg"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="759" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/40px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/60px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/80px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist">Wikinews has related news: <i><b><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikinews.org/wiki/Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez_out_as_Real_Madrid_appoints_Zidane_their_new_manager" title="wikinews:Rafael Benítez out as Real Madrid appoints Zidane their new manager">Rafael Benítez out as Real Madrid appoints Zidane their new manager</a></b></i></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On 3 June 2015, Benítez was confirmed as the new Real Madrid manager, signing a three-year contract.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Real Madrid remained unbeaten in the league until a 3–2 loss at Sevilla in the 11th matchday. This was followed by a 4–0 home loss in the first <a href="/wiki/El_Cl%C3%A1sico" title="El Clásico">Clásico</a> of the season against Barcelona. Real later played <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz_CF" title="Cádiz CF">Cádiz</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Copa_del_Rey#Round_of_32" title="2015–16 Copa del Rey">Copa del Rey Round of 32</a>, winning away 3–1 in the first leg. However, they fielded an ineligible player in <a href="/wiki/Denis_Cheryshev" title="Denis Cheryshev">Denis Cheryshev</a> as he was suspended for that match, resulting in the second leg being cancelled and Madrid being disqualified. Meanwhile, Real topped their <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_UEFA_Champions_League#Group_A" title="2015–16 UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League group</a> with 16 points.</p>
<p>On 4 January 2016, Benítez's contract was terminated following allegations of unpopularity with supporters, displeasure with players and a failure to get good results against top sides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> At the time of sacking, Real were third in La Liga, four points behind leaders Atlético Madrid and two points behind arch-rivals Barcelona, the latter who had a game in hand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newcastle_United">Newcastle United</span></h3>
<p>On 11 March 2016, Benítez was announced as the manager of relegation threatened <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>, signing on an initial three-year deal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> He suffered defeat in his first match in charge, losing 1–0 away to eventual champions <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a> on 14 March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Benítez would have to wait until 16 April for his first win in charge of <i>The Magpies</i>, recording a convincing 3–0 victory over <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swansea_City_F.C." title="Swansea City F.C.">Swansea City</a> in the Premier League.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>Newcastle ended the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Premier_League" title="2015–16 Premier League">season</a> with a six match unbeaten run, including a 5–1 final day defeat of third-place Tottenham Hotspur.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> However, the team was relegated to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship" title="Football League Championship">Football League Championship</a> due to rivals <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a> claiming 12 points from their final six fixtures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> On 25 May 2016, it was confirmed he would remain as manager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Relations_with_other_managers">Relations with other managers</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Zola_%26_Benitez_Upton_Park_09May09.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1575" data-file-width="2617" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Zola_%26_Benitez_Upton_Park_09May09.jpg/300px-Zola_%26_Benitez_Upton_Park_09May09.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Zola_%26_Benitez_Upton_Park_09May09.jpg/450px-Zola_%26_Benitez_Upton_Park_09May09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Zola_%26_Benitez_Upton_Park_09May09.jpg/600px-Zola_%26_Benitez_Upton_Park_09May09.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Zola_%26_Benitez_Upton_Park_09May09.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
With <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Ham_United" title="West Ham United">West Ham United</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Gianfranco_Zola" title="Gianfranco Zola">Gianfranco Zola</a> at <a href="/wiki/Boleyn_Ground" title="Boleyn Ground">Boleyn Ground</a> 9 May 2009.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Manchester_City-Liverpool--Pearce_and_Benitez.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="407" data-file-width="345" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Manchester_City-Liverpool--Pearce_and_Benitez.jpg/200px-Manchester_City-Liverpool--Pearce_and_Benitez.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Manchester_City-Liverpool--Pearce_and_Benitez.jpg/300px-Manchester_City-Liverpool--Pearce_and_Benitez.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/50/Manchester_City-Liverpool--Pearce_and_Benitez.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Manchester_City-Liverpool--Pearce_and_Benitez.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
With <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Pearce" title="Stuart Pearce">Stuart Pearce</a> at the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Manchester_Stadium" title="City of Manchester Stadium">City of Manchester Stadium</a>, 14 February 2007.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Benítez has had confrontations with both José Mourinho (Chelsea manager from 2004–2007) and Manchester United's Sir Alex Ferguson during his time in English football. Benítez made a number of suggestions during Mourinho's tenure as manager that <a href="/wiki/Roman_Abramovich" title="Roman Abramovich">Roman Abramovich</a>'s money had bought Chelsea's success, and the pair refused to shake hands after some matches (although Mourinho declared the feud to be over after a league game in 2006). When Mourinho exited Chelsea in 2007, Benítez said, "You know my relationship with him, it is better that I do not say anything," declining to comment as Ferguson and Arsenal manager <a href="/wiki/Ars%C3%A8ne_Wenger" title="Arsène Wenger">Arsène Wenger</a> had.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 9 January 2009, Benítez delivered a controversial appraisal of certain aspects of Sir Alex Ferguson's tenure, accusing Ferguson and Manchester United of being nervous because Liverpool were at the top of the league,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rafarant_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-rafarant-103">[103]</a></sup> then accused the Manchester United manager of not being punished for breaking <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">FA</a> rules, suggesting he was "the only manager in the league that cannot be punished for these things",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rafarant_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-rafarant-103">[103]</a></sup> referring to Ferguson not being punished following an FA charge for comments he made about officials <a href="/wiki/Martin_Atkinson" title="Martin Atkinson">Martin Atkinson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Keith_Hackett" title="Keith Hackett">Keith Hackett</a> following an <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> tie with <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fergpompey_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-fergpompey-104">[104]</a></sup> In his 2013 autobiography, Ferguson said that "Benitez bought badly and made the feud personal".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>Benítez has also had confrontations with <a href="/wiki/Sam_Allardyce" title="Sam Allardyce">Sam Allardyce</a> when he was manager of <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a>. When Allardyce was manager of Newcastle, he suggested Benítez would have been sacked had Liverpool's European form been as bad as their league form.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> In a match in April 2009 when Allardyce was manager of Blackburn, he accused Benítez of arrogance over a gesture he made when Fernando Torres scored Liverpool's second goal. Allardyce suggested that Benítez had signalled the game was over despite Liverpool only having a two-goal lead. This view was later supported by Sir Alex Ferguson. Benítez, however, later explained this gesture: he said he had previously told Xabi Alonso to take a short free-kick. This instruction was ignored, which resulted in a goal. Benítez said that he had jokingly signalled to Alonso to ignore his instructions and not that he thought the game was effectively over.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Management_style">Management style</span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-globalize" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="Globe icon." data-file-height="290" data-file-width="350" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/48px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/73px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/97px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 2x" width="48"/></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">The examples and perspective in this article <b>deal primarily with the United Kingdom and do not represent a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Countering_systemic_bias" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Countering systemic bias">worldwide view</a> of the subject</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">You may <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a>, discuss the issue on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez" title="Talk:Rafael Benítez">talk page</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Article_wizard" title="Wikipedia:Article wizard">create a new article</a>, as appropriate.</span> <small><i>(January 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Benítez has developed a reputation in English football as a hard man to please, with former Liverpool captain <a href="/wiki/Steven_Gerrard" title="Steven Gerrard">Steven Gerrard</a> admitting he longed for a "well done" from Benítez after good performances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Benítez's ruthlessness can also be seen in the way he disposed of all but Gerrard and <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Carragher" title="Jamie Carragher">Jamie Carragher</a> from his Champions League winning squad within four seasons, with penalty shoot-out hero <a href="/wiki/Jerzy_Dudek" title="Jerzy Dudek">Jerzy Dudek</a> made back-up goalkeeper the very season after the European triumph.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>Benítez's preferred formation is a 4–2–3–1 which he adopted during his time at Valencia and Liverpool. He has often been praised<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (May 2013)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> for his tactical acumen<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> particularly in European ties, setting his team up to exploit opposition weaknesses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> His calm demeanour and tactical changes at half time of the <a href="/wiki/2005_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2005 UEFA Champions League Final">2005 UEFA Champions League Final</a> were said to give players belief they could battle back from 3–0 down, although he had to correct his plans when it was pointed out to him his new formation would require 12 players on the pitch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Benítez often plays key players in unorthodox positions to suit a formation – notably converting both Steven Gerrard (in the 2005-06 season) and <a href="/wiki/Dirk_Kuyt" title="Dirk Kuyt">Dirk Kuyt</a> into right-wingers. As a right winger/midfielder, Steven Gerrard had the most productive seasons winning wise, claiming a Champions League title, and an FA Cup.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:305px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rafa_Benitez_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1975" data-file-width="2965" height="202" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Rafa_Benitez_2013.jpg/303px-Rafa_Benitez_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Rafa_Benitez_2013.jpg/455px-Rafa_Benitez_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Rafa_Benitez_2013.jpg/606px-Rafa_Benitez_2013.jpg 2x" width="303"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rafa_Benitez_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Benítez in 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Benítez is a firm believer in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Squad_rotation_system" title="Squad rotation system">squad rotation</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zonal_marking" title="Zonal marking">zonal marking</a>. Despite heavy criticism from the English press<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Benítez persisted with the reward of a Champions League and FA Cup triumph in his first two seasons. Benítez argued he needed to rotate his small squad to ensure key players were fit for the latter stages of these knockout competitions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>The tactic of zonal marking has been criticised by pundits when Liverpool concede from set-pieces<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> in spite of the fact that Benítez's squads are usually renowned for their defensive nature and low number of goals scored against them. Benítez stands by his tactic, pointing out that teams who <a href="/wiki/Marking_(association_football)#Man-to-man_marking" title="Marking (association football)">man-mark</a> concede just as many, if not more, goals from set pieces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>Benítez instigated a host of backroom changes at the end of the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="2008–09 Liverpool F.C. season">2008–09 season</a> to improve the club's youth development, including the appointment of club legend <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Dalglish" title="Kenny Dalglish">Kenny Dalglish</a> in a senior role at the academy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>Benítez's father, Francisco, worked as a hotelier. His mother is Rosario Maudes. Rosario was a big football fan and supported Real Madrid, while his father supported Atlético Madrid. Francisco died in December 2005 while Benítez was in Japan for the FIFA Club World Championship.</p>
<p>Rafael Benítez married Maria de Montserrat in 1998. They have two daughters, Claudia, who was born in Madrid in 1999, and Ágata who was born in Valencia in 2002. Benítez is fluent in Spanish, English and Italian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
